    11.

      12.

    13.

      14.

    15.

      16. 
      
        
    16.

    17.

    390. 
          
          
                  # We have some records loaded from the database (persisted) and some that are
        
      391. 
      
        
    391. 
          
          
                  # in-memory (memory). The same record may be represented in the persisted array
        
      392. 
      
        
    392. 
          
          
                  # and in the memory array.
        
      393. 
      
        
    393. 
          
          
                  #
        
      394. 
      
        
    394.

      395. 
      
        
    395. 
          
          
                  #
        
      396. 
      
        
    396. 
          
          
                  #   * The final array must not have duplicates
        
      397. 
      
        
    397. 
          
          
                  #   * The order of the persisted array is to be preserved
        
      398. 
      
        
    398. 
          
          
                  #   * Any changes made to attributes on objects in the memory array are to be preserved
        
      399. 
      
        
    399. 
          
          
                  #   * Otherwise, attributes should have the value found in the database
        
      400. 
      
        
    400. 
          1
          
                  def merge_target_lists(persisted, memory)
        
      401. 
      
        
    401. 
          
          
                    return persisted if memory.empty?
        
      402. 
      
        
    402.

      403.

      404. 
      
        
    404.

      405. 
      
        
    405.

      406. 
      
        
    406. 
          
          
                      # record rather than memory.at(memory.index(record)). The behavior is fixed in 1.9.
        
      407. 
      
        
    407. 
          
          
                      mem_index = memory.index(record)
        
      408. 
      
        
    408. 
          
          
          
        
      409. 
      
        
    409. 
          
          
                      if mem_index
        
      410. 
      
        
    410. 
          
          
                        mem_record = memory.delete_at(mem_index)
        
      411. 
      
        
    411. 
          
          
          
        
      412. 
      
        
    412. 
          
          
                        ((record.attribute_names & mem_record.attribute_names) - mem_record.changes.keys).each do |name|
        
      413. 
      
        
    413. 
          
          
                          mem_record[name] = record[name]
        
      414. 
      
        
    414. 
          
          
                        end
        
      415. 
      
        
    415. 
          
          
          
        
      416. 
      
        
    416.

      417.

      418.

                    persisted + memory

    423. 
          
          
                  end

                  def delete_or_destroy(records, method)

              # Note that this method actually runs the queries, since the results of some
        
      141. 
      
        
    141.

      142. 
      
        
    142.

      143. 
      
        
    143.

      144. 
      
        
    144. 
          
          
              # {Active Record Query Interface guide}[http://edgeguides.rubyonrails.org/active_record_querying.html#running-explain].

              def explain
        
      146. 
      
        
    146. 
          
          
                _, queries = collecting_queries_for_explain { exec_queries }
        
      147.

              def to_a
        
      151. 
      
        
    151. 
          
          
                # We monitor here the entire execution rather than individual SELECTs
        
      152. 
      
        
    152. 
          
          
                # because from the point of view of the user fetching the records of a
        
      153. 
      
        
    153. 
          
          
                # relation is a single unit of work. You want to know if this call takes
        
      154. 
      
        
    154. 
          
          
                # too long, not if the individual queries take too long.
        
      155. 
      
        
    155. 
          
          
                #
        
      156. 
      
        
    156. 
          
          
                # It could be the case that none of the queries involved surpass the
        
      157. 
      
        
    157. 
          
          
                # threshold, and at the same time the sum of them all does. The user
        
      158. 
      
        
    158. 
          
          
                # should get a query plan logged in that case.
        
      159. 
      
        
    159. 
          4
          
                logging_query_plan do
        
      160. 
      
        
    160. 
          4
          
                  exec_queries
        
      161. 
      
        
    161. 
          
          
                end
        
      162. 
      
        
    162. 
          
          
              end

              def exec_queries

          4
          
                return @records if loaded?
        
      166.

      167.

          4
          
                default_scoped = with_default_scope

      169. 
      
        
    169. 
          4
          
                if default_scoped.equal?(self)
        
      170. 
      
        
    170. 
          4
          
                  @records = if @readonly_value.nil? && !@klass.locking_enabled?
        
      171. 
      
        
    171. 
          4
          
                    eager_loading? ? find_with_associations : @klass.find_by_sql(arel, @bind_values)
        
      172. 
      
        
    172. 
          
          
                  else
        
      173. 
      
        
    173. 
          
          
                    IdentityMap.without do
        
      174. 
      
        
    174. 
          
          
                      eager_loading? ? find_with_associations : @klass.find_by_sql(arel, @bind_values)
        
      175. 
      
        
    175. 
          
          
                    end
        
      176. 
      
        
    176. 
          
          
                  end
        
      177.

      178. 
      
        
    178. 
          4
          
                  preload = @preload_values
        
      179. 
      
        
    179.

                  preload +=  @includes_values unless eager_loading?

                  preload.each do |associations|

                    ActiveRecord::Associations::Preloader.new(@records, associations).run

      184.

                  # @readonly_value is true only if set explicitly. @implicit_readonly is true if there
        
      185. 
      
        
    185. 
          
          
                  # are JOINS and no explicit SELECT.
        
      186. 
      
        
    186. 
          4
          
                  readonly = @readonly_value.nil? ? @implicit_readonly : @readonly_value
        
      187. 
      
        
    187. 
          4
          
                  @records.each { |record| record.readonly! } if readonly
        
      188. 
      
        
    188. 
          
          
                else
        
      189. 
      
        
    189. 
          
          
                  @records = default_scoped.to_a
        
      190.

                @loaded = true
        
      193. 
      
        
    193. 
          4
          
                @records

              end

              # Returns size of the records.

              def any?

                if block_given?

                  to_a.any? { |*block_args| yield(*block_args) }

    230. 
          
          
              # Scope all queries to the current scope.
        
      231. 
      
        
    231. 
          
          
              #
        
      232. 
      
        
    232. 
          
          
              # ==== Example
        
      233. 
      
        
    233. 
          
          
              #
        
      234. 
      
        
    234. 
          
          
              #   Comment.where(:post_id => 1).scoping do
        
      235. 
      
        
    235. 
          
          
              #     Comment.first # SELECT * FROM comments WHERE post_id = 1
        
      236. 
      
        
    236. 
          
          
              #   end
        
      237. 
      
        
    237. 
          
          
              #
        
      238. 
      
        
    238. 
          
          
              # Please check unscoped if you want to remove all previous scopes (including
        
      239. 
      
        
    239. 
          
          
              # the default_scope) during the execution of a block.
        
      240. 
      
        
    240. 
          1
          
              def scoping
        
      241. 
      
        
    241. 
          20
          
                @klass.with_scope(self, :overwrite) { yield }
        
      242. 
      
        
    242. 
          
          
              end
        
      243.

      244. 
      
        
    244. 
          
          
              # Updates all records with details given if they match a set of conditions supplied, limits and order can
        
      245. 
      
        
    245. 
          
          
              # also be supplied. This method constructs a single SQL UPDATE statement and sends it straight to the
        
      246. 
      
        
    246. 
          
          
              # database. It does not instantiate the involved models and it does not trigger Active Record callbacks
        
      247. 
      
        
    247. 
          
          
              # or validations.
        
      248. 
      
        
    248. 
          
          
              #
        
      249. 
      
        
    249. 
          
          
              # ==== Parameters
        
      250. 
      
        
    250. 
          
          
              #
        
      251. 
      
        
    251. 
          
          
              # * +updates+ - A string, array, or hash representing the SET part of an SQL statement.
        
      252. 
      
        
    252. 
          
          
              # * +conditions+ - A string, array, or hash representing the WHERE part of an SQL statement.
        
      253. 
      
        
    253. 
          
          
              #   See conditions in the intro.
        
      254. 
      
        
    254. 
          
          
              # * +options+ - Additional options are <tt>:limit</tt> and <tt>:order</tt>, see the examples for usage.
        
      255. 
      
        
    255. 
          
          
              #
        
      256. 
      
        
    256. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      257. 
      
        
    257. 
          
          
              #
        
      258. 
      
        
    258. 
          
          
              #   # Update all customers with the given attributes
        
      259. 
      
        
    259. 
          
          
              #   Customer.update_all :wants_email => true
        
      260. 
      
        
    260. 
          
          
              #
        
      261. 
      
        
    261. 
          
          
              #   # Update all books with 'Rails' in their title
        
      262. 
      
        
    262. 
          
          
              #   Book.update_all "author = 'David'", "title LIKE '%Rails%'"
        
      263. 
      
        
    263. 
          
          
              #
        
      264. 
      
        
    264. 
          
          
              #   # Update all avatars migrated more than a week ago
        
      265. 
      
        
    265. 
          
          
              #   Avatar.update_all ['migrated_at = ?', Time.now.utc], ['migrated_at > ?', 1.week.ago]
        
      266. 
      
        
    266. 
          
          
              #
        
      267. 
      
        
    267. 
          
          
              #   # Update all books that match conditions, but limit it to 5 ordered by date
        
      268. 
      
        
    268. 
          
          
              #   Book.update_all "author = 'David'", "title LIKE '%Rails%'", :order => 'created_at', :limit => 5
        
      269. 
      
        
    269. 
          
          
              #
        
      270. 
      
        
    270. 
          
          
              #   # Conditions from the current relation also works
        
      271. 
      
        
    271. 
          
          
              #   Book.where('title LIKE ?', '%Rails%').update_all(:author => 'David')
        
      272. 
      
        
    272. 
          
          
              #
        
      273. 
      
        
    273. 
          
          
              #   # The same idea applies to limit and order
        
      274. 
      
        
    274. 
          
          
              #   Book.where('title LIKE ?', '%Rails%').order(:created_at).limit(5).update_all(:author => 'David')
        
      275. 
      
        
    275. 
          1
          
              def update_all(updates, conditions = nil, options = {})
        
      276. 
      
        
    276. 
          
          
                IdentityMap.repository[symbolized_base_class].clear if IdentityMap.enabled?
        
      277. 
      
        
    277. 
          
          
                if conditions || options.present?
        
      278. 
      
        
    278. 
          
          
                  where(conditions).apply_finder_options(options.slice(:limit, :order)).update_all(updates)
        
      279. 
      
        
    279. 
          
          
                else
        
      280. 
      
        
    280. 
          
          
                  stmt = Arel::UpdateManager.new(arel.engine)
        
      281. 
      
        
    281. 
          
          
          
        
      282. 
      
        
    282. 
          
          
                  stmt.set Arel.sql(@klass.send(:sanitize_sql_for_assignment, updates))
        
      283. 
      
        
    283. 
          
          
                  stmt.table(table)
        
      284. 
      
        
    284. 
          
          
                  stmt.key = table[primary_key]
        
      285. 
      
        
    285. 
          
          
          
        
      286. 
      
        
    286. 
          
          
                  if joins_values.any?
        
      287. 
      
        
    287. 
          
          
                    @klass.connection.join_to_update(stmt, arel)
        
      288. 
      
        
    288. 
          
          
                  else
        
      289. 
      
        
    289. 
          
          
                    stmt.take(arel.limit)
        
      290. 
      
        
    290. 
          
          
                    stmt.order(*arel.orders)
        
      291. 
      
        
    291. 
          
          
                    stmt.wheres = arel.constraints
        
      292. 
      
        
    292. 
          
          
                  end
        
      293. 
      
        
    293. 
          
          
          
        
      294. 
      
        
    294. 
          
          
                  @klass.connection.update stmt, 'SQL', bind_values
        
      295. 
      
        
    295. 
          
          
                end
        
      296. 
      
        
    296. 
          
          
              end
        
      297. 
      
        
    297. 
          
          
          
        
      298. 
      
        
    298. 
          
          
              # Updates an object (or multiple objects) and saves it to the database, if validations pass.
        
      299. 
      
        
    299. 
          
          
              # The resulting object is returned whether the object was saved successfully to the database or not.
        
      300. 
      
        
    300. 
          
          
              #
        
      301. 
      
        
    301. 
          
          
              # ==== Parameters
        
      302. 
      
        
    302. 
          
          
              #
        
      303. 
      
        
    303. 
          
          
              # * +id+ - This should be the id or an array of ids to be updated.
        
      304. 
      
        
    304. 
          
          
              # * +attributes+ - This should be a hash of attributes or an array of hashes.
        
      305. 
      
        
    305. 
          
          
              #
        
      306. 
      
        
    306. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      307. 
      
        
    307. 
          
          
              #
        
      308. 
      
        
    308. 
          
          
              #   # Updates one record
        
      309. 
      
        
    309. 
          
          
              #   Person.update(15, :user_name => 'Samuel', :group => 'expert')
        
      310. 
      
        
    310. 
          
          
              #
        
      311. 
      
        
    311. 
          
          
              #   # Updates multiple records
        
      312. 
      
        
    312. 
          
          
              #   people = { 1 => { "first_name" => "David" }, 2 => { "first_name" => "Jeremy" } }
        
      313. 
      
        
    313. 
          
          
              #   Person.update(people.keys, people.values)
        
      314. 
      
        
    314. 
          1
          
              def update(id, attributes)
        
      315. 
      
        
    315. 
          
          
                if id.is_a?(Array)
        
      316. 
      
        
    316. 
          
          
                  id.each.with_index.map {|one_id, idx| update(one_id, attributes[idx])}
        
      317. 
      
        
    317. 
          
          
                else
        
      318. 
      
        
    318. 
          
          
                  object = find(id)
        
      319. 
      
        
    319. 
          
          
                  object.update_attributes(attributes)
        
      320. 
      
        
    320. 
          
          
                  object
        
      321. 
      
        
    321. 
          
          
                end
        
      322. 
      
        
    322. 
          
          
              end
        
      323. 
      
        
    323. 
          
          
          
        
      324. 
      
        
    324. 
          
          
              # Destroys the records matching +conditions+ by instantiating each
        
      325. 
      
        
    325. 
          
          
              # record and calling its +destroy+ method. Each object's callbacks are
        
      326. 
      
        
    326. 
          
          
              # executed (including <tt>:dependent</tt> association options and
        
      327. 
      
        
    327. 
          
          
              # +before_destroy+/+after_destroy+ Observer methods). Returns the
        
      328. 
      
        
    328. 
          
          
              # collection of objects that were destroyed; each will be frozen, to
        
      329. 
      
        
    329. 
          
          
              # reflect that no changes should be made (since they can't be
        
      330. 
      
        
    330. 
          
          
              # persisted).
        
      331. 
      
        
    331. 
          
          
              #
        
      332. 
      
        
    332. 
          
          
              # Note: Instantiation, callback execution, and deletion of each
        
      333. 
      
        
    333. 
          
          
              # record can be time consuming when you're removing many records at
        
      334. 
      
        
    334. 
          
          
              # once. It generates at least one SQL +DELETE+ query per record (or
        
      335. 
      
        
    335. 
          
          
              # possibly more, to enforce your callbacks). If you want to delete many
        
      336. 
      
        
    336. 
          
          
              # rows quickly, without concern for their associations or callbacks, use
        
      337. 
      
        
    337. 
          
          
              # +delete_all+ instead.
        
      338. 
      
        
    338. 
          
          
              #
        
      339. 
      
        
    339. 
          
          
              # ==== Parameters
        
      340. 
      
        
    340. 
          
          
              #
        
      341. 
      
        
    341. 
          
          
              # * +conditions+ - A string, array, or hash that specifies which records
        
      342. 
      
        
    342. 
          
          
              #   to destroy. If omitted, all records are destroyed. See the
        
      343. 
      
        
    343. 
          
          
              #   Conditions section in the introduction to ActiveRecord::Base for
        
      344. 
      
        
    344. 
          
          
              #   more information.
        
      345. 
      
        
    345. 
          
          
              #
        
      346. 
      
        
    346. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      347. 
      
        
    347. 
          
          
              #
        
      348. 
      
        
    348. 
          
          
              #   Person.destroy_all("last_login < '2004-04-04'")
        
      349. 
      
        
    349. 
          
          
              #   Person.destroy_all(:status => "inactive")
        
      350. 
      
        
    350. 
          
          
              #   Person.where(:age => 0..18).destroy_all
        
      351. 
      
        
    351. 
          1
          
              def destroy_all(conditions = nil)
        
      352. 
      
        
    352. 
          
          
                if conditions
        
      353. 
      
        
    353. 
          
          
                  where(conditions).destroy_all
        
      354. 
      
        
    354. 
          
          
                else
        
      355. 
      
        
    355. 
          
          
                  to_a.each {|object| object.destroy }.tap { reset }
        
      356. 
      
        
    356. 
          
          
                end
        
      357. 
      
        
    357. 
          
          
              end
        
      358. 
      
        
    358. 
          
          
          
        
      359. 
      
        
    359. 
          
          
              # Destroy an object (or multiple objects) that has the given id, the object is instantiated first,
        
      360. 
      
        
    360. 
          
          
              # therefore all callbacks and filters are fired off before the object is deleted. This method is
        
      361. 
      
        
    361. 
          
          
              # less efficient than ActiveRecord#delete but allows cleanup methods and other actions to be run.
        
      362. 
      
        
    362. 
          
          
              #
        
      363. 
      
        
    363. 
          
          
              # This essentially finds the object (or multiple objects) with the given id, creates a new object
        
      364. 
      
        
    364. 
          
          
              # from the attributes, and then calls destroy on it.
        
      365. 
      
        
    365. 
          
          
              #
        
      366. 
      
        
    366. 
          
          
              # ==== Parameters
        
      367. 
      
        
    367. 
          
          
              #
        
      368. 
      
        
    368. 
          
          
              # * +id+ - Can be either an Integer or an Array of Integers.
        
      369. 
      
        
    369. 
          
          
              #
        
      370. 
      
        
    370. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      371. 
      
        
    371. 
          
          
              #
        
      372. 
      
        
    372. 
          
          
              #   # Destroy a single object
        
      373. 
      
        
    373. 
          
          
              #   Todo.destroy(1)
        
      374. 
      
        
    374. 
          
          
              #
        
      375. 
      
        
    375. 
          
          
              #   # Destroy multiple objects
        
      376. 
      
        
    376. 
          
          
              #   todos = [1,2,3]
        
      377. 
      
        
    377. 
          
          
              #   Todo.destroy(todos)
        
      378. 
      
        
    378. 
          1
          
              def destroy(id)
        
      379. 
      
        
    379. 
          
          
                if id.is_a?(Array)
        
      380. 
      
        
    380. 
          
          
                  id.map { |one_id| destroy(one_id) }
        
      381. 
      
        
    381. 
          
          
                else
        
      382. 
      
        
    382. 
          
          
                  find(id).destroy
        
      383. 
      
        
    383. 
          
          
                end
        
      384. 
      
        
    384. 
          
          
              end
        
      385. 
      
        
    385. 
          
          
          
        
      386. 
      
        
    386. 
          
          
              # Deletes the records matching +conditions+ without instantiating the records first, and hence not
        
      387. 
      
        
    387. 
          
          
              # calling the +destroy+ method nor invoking callbacks. This is a single SQL DELETE statement that
        
      388. 
      
        
    388. 
          
          
              # goes straight to the database, much more efficient than +destroy_all+. Be careful with relations
        
      389. 
      
        
    389. 
          
          
              # though, in particular <tt>:dependent</tt> rules defined on associations are not honored. Returns
        
      390. 
      
        
    390. 
          
          
              # the number of rows affected.
        
      391. 
      
        
    391. 
          
          
              #
        
      392. 
      
        
    392. 
          
          
              # ==== Parameters
        
      393. 
      
        
    393. 
          
          
              #
        
      394. 
      
        
    394. 
          
          
              # * +conditions+ - Conditions are specified the same way as with +find+ method.
        
      395. 
      
        
    395. 
          
          
              #
        
      396.

              # Count operates using three different approaches.
        
      7. 
      
        
    7. 
          
          
              #
        
      8. 
      
        
    8. 
          
          
              # * Count all: By not passing any parameters to count, it will return a count of all the rows for the model.
        
      9. 
      
        
    9. 
          
          
              # * Count using column: By passing a column name to count, it will return a count of all the
        
      10. 
      
        
    10. 
          
          
              #   rows for the model with supplied column present.
        
      11. 
      
        
    11. 
          
          
              # * Count using options will find the row count matched by the options used.
        
      12. 
      
        
    12. 
          
          
              #
        
      13. 
      
        
    13. 
          
          
              # The third approach, count using options, accepts an option hash as the only parameter. The options are:
        
      14. 
      
        
    14. 
          
          
              #
        
      15. 
      
        
    15. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:conditions</tt>: An SQL fragment like "administrator = 1" or [ "user_name = ?", username ].
        
      16. 
      
        
    16. 
          
          
              #   See conditions in the intro to ActiveRecord::Base.
        
      17. 
      
        
    17. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:joins</tt>: Either an SQL fragment for additional joins like "LEFT JOIN comments ON comments.post_id = id"
        
      18. 
      
        
    18. 
          
          
              #   (rarely needed) or named associations in the same form used for the <tt>:include</tt> option, which will
        
      19. 
      
        
    19. 
          
          
              #   perform an INNER JOIN on the associated table(s). If the value is a string, then the records
        
      20. 
      
        
    20. 
          
          
              #   will be returned read-only since they will have attributes that do not correspond to the table's columns.
        
      21. 
      
        
    21. 
          
          
              #   Pass <tt>:readonly => false</tt> to override.
        
      22. 
      
        
    22. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:include</tt>: Named associations that should be loaded alongside using LEFT OUTER JOINs.
        
      23. 
      
        
    23. 
          
          
              #   The symbols named refer to already defined associations. When using named associations, count
        
      24. 
      
        
    24. 
          
          
              #   returns the number of DISTINCT items for the model you're counting.
        
      25. 
      
        
    25. 
          
          
              #   See eager loading under Associations.
        
      26. 
      
        
    26. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:order</tt>: An SQL fragment like "created_at DESC, name" (really only used with GROUP BY calculations).
        
      27. 
      
        
    27. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:group</tt>: An attribute name by which the result should be grouped. Uses the GROUP BY SQL-clause.
        
      28. 
      
        
    28. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:select</tt>: By default, this is * as in SELECT * FROM, but can be changed if you, for example,
        
      29. 
      
        
    29. 
          
          
              #   want to do a join but not include the joined columns.
        
      30. 
      
        
    30. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:distinct</tt>: Set this to true to make this a distinct calculation, such as
        
      31. 
      
        
    31. 
          
          
              #   SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT posts.id) ...
        
      32. 
      
        
    32. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:from</tt> - By default, this is the table name of the class, but can be changed to an
        
      33. 
      
        
    33. 
          
          
              #   alternate table name (or even the name of a database view).
        
      34. 
      
        
    34. 
          
          
              #
        
      35. 
      
        
    35. 
          
          
              # Examples for counting all:
        
      36. 
      
        
    36. 
          
          
              #   Person.count         # returns the total count of all people
        
      37. 
      
        
    37. 
          
          
              #
        
      38. 
      
        
    38. 
          
          
              # Examples for counting by column:
        
      39. 
      
        
    39. 
          
          
              #   Person.count(:age)  # returns the total count of all people whose age is present in database
        
      40. 
      
        
    40. 
          
          
              #
        
      41. 
      
        
    41. 
          
          
              # Examples for count with options:
        
      42. 
      
        
    42. 
          
          
              #   Person.count(:conditions => "age > 26")
        
      43. 
      
        
    43. 
          
          
              #
        
      44. 
      
        
    44. 
          
          
              #   # because of the named association, it finds the DISTINCT count using LEFT OUTER JOIN.
        
      45. 
      
        
    45. 
          
          
              #   Person.count(:conditions => "age > 26 AND job.salary > 60000", :include => :job)
        
      46. 
      
        
    46. 
          
          
              #
        
      47. 
      
        
    47. 
          
          
              #   # finds the number of rows matching the conditions and joins.
        
      48. 
      
        
    48. 
          
          
              #   Person.count(:conditions => "age > 26 AND job.salary > 60000",
        
      49. 
      
        
    49. 
          
          
              #                :joins => "LEFT JOIN jobs on jobs.person_id = person.id")
        
      50. 
      
        
    50. 
          
          
              #
        
      51. 
      
        
    51. 
          
          
              #   Person.count('id', :conditions => "age > 26") # Performs a COUNT(id)
        
      52. 
      
        
    52. 
          
          
              #   Person.count(:all, :conditions => "age > 26") # Performs a COUNT(*) (:all is an alias for '*')
        
      53. 
      
        
    53. 
          
          
              #
        
      54. 
      
        
    54. 
          
          
              # Note: <tt>Person.count(:all)</tt> will not work because it will use <tt>:all</tt> as the condition.
        
      55. 
      
        
    55. 
          
          
              # Use Person.count instead.
        
      56. 
      
        
    56. 
          1
          
              def count(column_name = nil, options = {})
        
      57. 
      
        
    57. 
          
          
                column_name, options = nil, column_name if column_name.is_a?(Hash)
        
      58. 
      
        
    58. 
          
          
                calculate(:count, column_name, options)
        
      59. 
      
        
    59. 
          
          
              end
        
      60. 
      
        
    60. 
          
          
          
        
      61. 
      
        
    61. 
          
          
              # Calculates the average value on a given column. Returns +nil+ if there's
        
      62. 
      
        
    62. 
          
          
              # no row. See +calculate+ for examples with options.
        
      63. 
      
        
    63. 
          
          
              #
        
      64. 
      
        
    64. 
          
          
              #   Person.average('age') # => 35.8
        
      65. 
      
        
    65. 
          1
          
              def average(column_name, options = {})
        
      66. 
      
        
    66. 
          
          
                calculate(:average, column_name, options)
        
      67. 
      
        
    67. 
          
          
              end
        
      68. 
      
        
    68. 
          
          
          
        
      69. 
      
        
    69. 
          
          
              # Calculates the minimum value on a given column. The value is returned
        
      70. 
      
        
    70. 
          
          
              # with the same data type of the column, or +nil+ if there's no row. See
        
      71. 
      
        
    71. 
          
          
              # +calculate+ for examples with options.
        
      72. 
      
        
    72. 
          
          
              #
        
      73. 
      
        
    73. 
          
          
              #   Person.minimum('age') # => 7
        
      74. 
      
        
    74. 
          1
          
              def minimum(column_name, options = {})
        
      75. 
      
        
    75. 
          
          
                calculate(:minimum, column_name, options)
        
      76. 
      
        
    76. 
          
          
              end
        
      77. 
      
        
    77. 
          
          
          
        
      78. 
      
        
    78. 
          
          
              # Calculates the maximum value on a given column. The value is returned
        
      79. 
      
        
    79. 
          
          
              # with the same data type of the column, or +nil+ if there's no row. See
        
      80. 
      
        
    80. 
          
          
              # +calculate+ for examples with options.
        
      81. 
      
        
    81. 
          
          
              #
        
      82. 
      
        
    82. 
          
          
              #   Person.maximum('age') # => 93
        
      83. 
      
        
    83. 
          1
          
              def maximum(column_name, options = {})
        
      84. 
      
        
    84. 
          
          
                calculate(:maximum, column_name, options)
        
      85. 
      
        
    85. 
          
          
              end
        
      86. 
      
        
    86. 
          
          
          
        
      87. 
      
        
    87. 
          
          
              # Calculates the sum of values on a given column. The value is returned
        
      88. 
      
        
    88. 
          
          
              # with the same data type of the column, 0 if there's no row. See
        
      89. 
      
        
    89. 
          
          
              # +calculate+ for examples with options.
        
      90. 
      
        
    90. 
          
          
              #
        
      91. 
      
        
    91. 
          
          
              #   Person.sum('age') # => 4562
        
      92. 
      
        
    92. 
          1
          
              def sum(*args)
        
      93. 
      
        
    93. 
          
          
                if block_given?
        
      94. 
      
        
    94. 
          
          
                  self.to_a.sum(*args) {|*block_args| yield(*block_args)}
        
      95. 
      
        
    95. 
          
          
                else
        
      96. 
      
        
    96. 
          
          
                  calculate(:sum, *args)
        
      97. 
      
        
    97. 
          
          
                end
        
      98. 
      
        
    98. 
          
          
              end
        
      99. 
      
        
    99. 
          
          
          
        
      100. 
      
        
    100. 
          
          
              # This calculates aggregate values in the given column. Methods for count, sum, average,
        
      101. 
      
        
    101. 
          
          
              # minimum, and maximum have been added as shortcuts. Options such as <tt>:conditions</tt>,
        
      102. 
      
        
    102. 
          
          
              # <tt>:order</tt>, <tt>:group</tt>, <tt>:having</tt>, and <tt>:joins</tt> can be passed to customize the query.
        
      103. 
      
        
    103. 
          
          
              #
        
      104. 
      
        
    104. 
          
          
              # There are two basic forms of output:
        
      105. 
      
        
    105. 
          
          
              #   * Single aggregate value: The single value is type cast to Fixnum for COUNT, Float
        
      106. 
      
        
    106. 
          
          
              #     for AVG, and the given column's type for everything else.
        
      107. 
      
        
    107. 
          
          
              #   * Grouped values: This returns an ordered hash of the values and groups them by the
        
      108. 
      
        
    108. 
          
          
              #     <tt>:group</tt> option. It takes either a column name, or the name of a belongs_to association.
        
      109. 
      
        
    109. 
          
          
              #
        
      110. 
      
        
    110. 
          
          
              #       values = Person.maximum(:age, :group => 'last_name')
        
      111. 
      
        
    111. 
          
          
              #       puts values["Drake"]
        
      112. 
      
        
    112. 
          
          
              #       => 43
        
      113. 
      
        
    113. 
          
          
              #
        
      114. 
      
        
    114. 
          
          
              #       drake  = Family.find_by_last_name('Drake')
        
      115. 
      
        
    115. 
          
          
              #       values = Person.maximum(:age, :group => :family) # Person belongs_to :family
        
      116. 
      
        
    116. 
          
          
              #       puts values[drake]
        
      117. 
      
        
    117. 
          
          
              #       => 43
        
      118. 
      
        
    118. 
          
          
              #
        
      119. 
      
        
    119. 
          
          
              #       values.each do |family, max_age|
        
      120. 
      
        
    120. 
          
          
              #       ...
        
      121. 
      
        
    121. 
          
          
              #       end
        
      122. 
      
        
    122. 
          
          
              #
        
      123. 
      
        
    123. 
          
          
              # Options:
        
      124. 
      
        
    124. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:conditions</tt> - An SQL fragment like "administrator = 1" or [ "user_name = ?", username ].
        
      125. 
      
        
    125. 
          
          
              #   See conditions in the intro to ActiveRecord::Base.
        
      126. 
      
        
    126. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:include</tt>: Eager loading, see Associations for details. Since calculations don't load anything,
        
      127. 
      
        
    127. 
          
          
              #   the purpose of this is to access fields on joined tables in your conditions, order, or group clauses.
        
      128. 
      
        
    128. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:joins</tt> - An SQL fragment for additional joins like "LEFT JOIN comments ON comments.post_id = id".
        
      129. 
      
        
    129. 
          
          
              #   (Rarely needed).
        
      130. 
      
        
    130. 
          
          
              #   The records will be returned read-only since they will have attributes that do not correspond to the
        
      131. 
      
        
    131. 
          
          
              #   table's columns.
        
      132. 
      
        
    132. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:order</tt> - An SQL fragment like "created_at DESC, name" (really only used with GROUP BY calculations).
        
      133. 
      
        
    133. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:group</tt> - An attribute name by which the result should be grouped. Uses the GROUP BY SQL-clause.
        
      134. 
      
        
    134. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:select</tt> - By default, this is * as in SELECT * FROM, but can be changed if you for example
        
      135. 
      
        
    135. 
          
          
              #   want to do a join, but not include the joined columns.
        
      136. 
      
        
    136. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:distinct</tt> - Set this to true to make this a distinct calculation, such as
        
      137. 
      
        
    137. 
          
          
              #   SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT posts.id) ...
        
      138. 
      
        
    138. 
          
          
              #
        
      139. 
      
        
    139. 
          
          
              # Examples:
        
      140. 
      
        
    140. 
          
          
              #   Person.calculate(:count, :all) # The same as Person.count
        
      141. 
      
        
    141. 
          
          
              #   Person.average(:age) # SELECT AVG(age) FROM people...
        
      142. 
      
        
    142. 
          
          
              #   Person.minimum(:age, :conditions => ['last_name != ?', 'Drake']) # Selects the minimum age for
        
      143. 
      
        
    143. 
          
          
              #                                                                    # everyone with a last name other than 'Drake'
        
      144. 
      
        
    144. 
          
          
              #
        
      145. 
      
        
    145. 
          
          
              #   # Selects the minimum age for any family without any minors
        
      146. 
      
        
    146. 
          
          
              #   Person.minimum(:age, :having => 'min(age) > 17', :group => :last_name)
        
      147. 
      
        
    147. 
          
          
              #
        
      148. 
      
        
    148. 
          
          
              #   Person.sum("2 * age")
        
      149. 
      
        
    149. 
          1
          
              def calculate(operation, column_name, options = {})
        
      150. 
      
        
    150. 
          
          
                if options.except(:distinct).present?
        
      151. 
      
        
    151. 
          
          
                  apply_finder_options(options.except(:distinct)).calculate(operation, column_name, :distinct => options[:distinct])
        
      152. 
      
        
    152. 
          
          
                else
        
      153. 
      
        
    153. 
          
          
                  relation = with_default_scope
        
      154. 
      
        
    154. 
          
          
          
        
      155. 
      
        
    155. 
          
          
                  if relation.equal?(self)
        
      156. 
      
        
    156. 
          
          
                    if eager_loading? || (includes_values.present? && references_eager_loaded_tables?)
        
      157. 
      
        
    157. 
          
          
                      construct_relation_for_association_calculations.calculate(operation, column_name, options)
        
      158. 
      
        
    158. 
          
          
                    else
        
      159. 
      
        
    159. 
          
          
                      perform_calculation(operation, column_name, options)
        
      160. 
      
        
    160. 
          
          
                    end
        
      161. 
      
        
    161. 
          
          
                  else
        
      162. 
      
        
    162. 
          
          
                    relation.calculate(operation, column_name, options)
        
      163. 
      
        
    163. 
          
          
                  end
        
      164. 
      
        
    164. 
          
          
                end
        
      165. 
      
        
    165. 
          
          
              rescue ThrowResult
        
      166. 
      
        
    166. 
          
          
                0
        
      167. 
      
        
    167. 
          
          
              end
        
      168. 
      
        
    168. 
          
          
          
        
      169. 
      
        
    169. 
          
          
              # This method is designed to perform select by a single column as direct SQL query
        
      170. 
      
        
    170. 
          
          
              # Returns <tt>Array</tt> with values of the specified column name
        
      171. 
      
        
    171. 
          
          
              # The values has same data type as column.
        
      172. 
      
        
    172. 
          
          
              #
        
      173. 
      
        
    173. 
          
          
              # Examples:
        
      174. 
      
        
    174. 
          
          
              #
        
      175. 
      
        
    175. 
          
          
              #   Person.pluck(:id) # SELECT people.id FROM people
        
      176. 
      
        
    176. 
          
          
              #   Person.uniq.pluck(:role) # SELECT DISTINCT role FROM people
        
      177. 
      
        
    177. 
          
          
              #   Person.where(:confirmed => true).limit(5).pluck(:id)
        
      178. 
      
        
    178. 
          
          
              #
        
      179. 
      
        
    179. 
          1
          
              def pluck(column_name)
        
      180. 
      
        
    180. 
          
          
                if column_name.is_a?(Symbol) && column_names.include?(column_name.to_s)
        
      181. 
      
        
    181. 
          
          
                  column_name = "#{connection.quote_table_name(table_name)}.#{connection.quote_column_name(column_name)}"
        
      182. 
      
        
    182. 
          
          
                else
        
      183. 
      
        
    183. 
          
          
                  column_name = column_name.to_s
        
      184. 
      
        
    184. 
          
          
                end
        
      185. 
      
        
    185. 
          
          
          
        
      186. 
      
        
    186. 
          
          
                relation = clone
        
      187. 
      
        
    187. 
          
          
                relation.select_values = [column_name]
        
      188. 
      
        
    188. 
          
          
                klass.connection.select_all(relation.arel).map! do |attributes|
        
      189. 
      
        
    189. 
          
          
                  klass.type_cast_attribute(attributes.keys.first, klass.initialize_attributes(attributes))
        
      190. 
      
        
    190. 
          
          
                end
        
      191. 
      
        
    191. 
          
          
              end
        
      192. 
      
        
    192. 
          
          
          
        
      193. 
      
        
    193. 
          1
          
              private
        
      194. 
      
        
    194. 
          
          
          
        
      195. 
      
        
    195. 
          1
          
              def perform_calculation(operation, column_name, options = {})
        
      196. 
      
        
    196. 
          
          
                operation = operation.to_s.downcase
        
      197. 
      
        
    197. 
          
          
          
        
      198. 
      
        
    198. 
          
          
                # If #count is used in conjuction with #uniq it is considered distinct. (eg. relation.uniq.count)
        
      199. 
      
        
    199. 
          
          
                distinct = options[:distinct] || self.uniq_value
        
      200. 
      
        
    200. 
          
          
          
        
      201. 
      
        
    201. 
          
          
                if operation == "count"
        
      202. 
      
        
    202. 
          
          
                  column_name ||= (select_for_count || :all)
        
      203. 
      
        
    203. 
          
          
          
        
      204. 
      
        
    204. 
          
          
                  unless arel.ast.grep(Arel::Nodes::OuterJoin).empty?
        
      205. 
      
        
    205. 
          
          
                    distinct = true
        
      206. 
      
        
    206. 
          
          
                  end
        
      207. 
      
        
    207. 
          
          
          
        
      208. 
      
        
    208. 
          
          
                  column_name = primary_key if column_name == :all && distinct
        
      209. 
      
        
    209. 
          
          
          
        
      210. 
      
        
    210. 
          
          
                  distinct = nil if column_name =~ /\s*DISTINCT\s+/i
        
      211. 
      
        
    211. 
          
          
                end
        
      212. 
      
        
    212. 
          
          
          
        
      213. 
      
        
    213. 
          
          
                if @group_values.any?
        
      214. 
      
        
    214. 
          
          
                  execute_grouped_calculation(operation, column_name, distinct)
        
      215. 
      
        
    215. 
          
          
                else
        
      216. 
      
        
    216. 
          
          
                  execute_simple_calculation(operation, column_name, distinct)
        
      217. 
      
        
    217. 
          
          
                end
        
      218. 
      
        
    218. 
          
          
              end
        
      219. 
      
        
    219. 
          
          
          
        
      220. 
      
        
    220. 
          1
          
              def aggregate_column(column_name)
        
      221. 
      
        
    221. 
          
          
                if @klass.column_names.include?(column_name.to_s)
        
      222. 
      
        
    222. 
          
          
                  Arel::Attribute.new(@klass.unscoped.table, column_name)
        
      223. 
      
        
    223. 
          
          
                else
        
      224. 
      
        
    224. 
          
          
                  Arel.sql(column_name == :all ? "*" : column_name.to_s)
        
      225. 
      
        
    225. 
          
          
                end
        
      226. 
      
        
    226. 
          
          
              end
        
      227. 
      
        
    227. 
          
          
          
        
      228. 
      
        
    228. 
          1
          
              def operation_over_aggregate_column(column, operation, distinct)
        
      229. 
      
        
    229. 
          
          
                operation == 'count' ? column.count(distinct) : column.send(operation)
        
      230. 
      
        
    230. 
          
          
              end
        
      231. 
      
        
    231. 
          
          
          
        
      232. 
      
        
    232. 
          1
          
              def execute_simple_calculation(operation, column_name, distinct) #:nodoc:
        
      233. 
      
        
    233. 
          
          
                # Postgresql doesn't like ORDER BY when there are no GROUP BY
        
      234. 
      
        
    234. 
          
          
                relation = reorder(nil)
        
      235. 
      
        
    235. 
          
          
          
        
      236. 
      
        
    236. 
          
          
                if operation == "count" && (relation.limit_value || relation.offset_value)
        
      237. 
      
        
    237. 
          
          
                  # Shortcut when limit is zero.
        
      238. 
      
        
    238. 
          
          
                  return 0 if relation.limit_value == 0
        
      239. 
      
        
    239. 
          
          
          
        
      240. 
      
        
    240. 
          
          
                  query_builder = build_count_subquery(relation, column_name, distinct)
        
      241. 
      
        
    241. 
          
          
                else
        
      242. 
      
        
    242. 
          
          
                  column = aggregate_column(column_name)
        
      243. 
      
        
    243. 
          
          
          
        
      244. 
      
        
    244. 
          
          
                  select_value = operation_over_aggregate_column(column, operation, distinct)
        
      245. 
      
        
    245. 
          
          
          
        
      246. 
      
        
    246. 
          
          
                  relation.select_values = [select_value]
        
      247. 
      
        
    247. 
          
          
          
        
      248. 
      
        
    248. 
          
          
                  query_builder = relation.arel
        
      249. 
      
        
    249. 
          
          
                end
        
      250. 
      
        
    250. 
          
          
          
        
      251. 
      
        
    251. 
          
          
                type_cast_calculated_value(@klass.connection.select_value(query_builder), column_for(column_name), operation)
        
      252. 
      
        
    252. 
          
          
              end
        
      253. 
      
        
    253. 
          
          
          
        
      254. 
      
        
    254. 
          1
          
              def execute_grouped_calculation(operation, column_name, distinct) #:nodoc:
        
      255. 
      
        
    255. 
          
          
                group_attrs = @group_values
        
      256. 
      
        
    256. 
          
          
          
        
      257. 
      
        
    257. 
          
          
                if group_attrs.first.respond_to?(:to_sym)
        
      258. 
      
        
    258. 
          
          
                  association  = @klass.reflect_on_association(group_attrs.first.to_sym)
        
      259. 
      
        
    259. 
          
          
                  associated   = group_attrs.size == 1 && association && association.macro == :belongs_to # only count belongs_to associations

              def build_count_subquery(relation, column_name, distinct)
        
      361. 
      
        
    361. 
          
          
                column_alias = Arel.sql('count_column')

      367.

      368. 
      
        
    368. 
          
          
                sm = Arel::SelectManager.new relation.engine
        
      369. 
      
        
    369.

      370. 
      
        
    370.

      371.

              end

          module ActiveRecord

            module FinderMethods

    6. 
          
          
              # Find operates with four different retrieval approaches:
        
      7. 
      
        
    7. 
          
          
              #
        
      8. 
      
        
    8. 
          
          
              # * Find by id - This can either be a specific id (1), a list of ids (1, 5, 6), or an array of ids ([5, 6, 10]).
        
      9. 
      
        
    9. 
          
          
              #   If no record can be found for all of the listed ids, then RecordNotFound will be raised.
        
      10. 
      
        
    10. 
          
          
              # * Find first - This will return the first record matched by the options used. These options can either be specific
        
      11. 
      
        
    11. 
          
          
              #   conditions or merely an order. If no record can be matched, +nil+ is returned. Use
        
      12. 
      
        
    12. 
          
          
              #   <tt>Model.find(:first, *args)</tt> or its shortcut <tt>Model.first(*args)</tt>.
        
      13. 
      
        
    13. 
          
          
              # * Find last - This will return the last record matched by the options used. These options can either be specific
        
      14. 
      
        
    14. 
          
          
              #   conditions or merely an order. If no record can be matched, +nil+ is returned. Use
        
      15. 
      
        
    15. 
          
          
              #   <tt>Model.find(:last, *args)</tt> or its shortcut <tt>Model.last(*args)</tt>.
        
      16. 
      
        
    16. 
          
          
              # * Find all - This will return all the records matched by the options used.
        
      17. 
      
        
    17. 
          
          
              #   If no records are found, an empty array is returned. Use
        
      18. 
      
        
    18. 
          
          
              #   <tt>Model.find(:all, *args)</tt> or its shortcut <tt>Model.all(*args)</tt>.
        
      19. 
      
        
    19. 
          
          
              #
        
      20. 
      
        
    20. 
          
          
              # All approaches accept an options hash as their last parameter.
        
      21. 
      
        
    21. 
          
          
              #
        
      22. 
      
        
    22. 
          
          
              # ==== Options
        
      23. 
      
        
    23. 
          
          
              #
        
      24. 
      
        
    24. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:conditions</tt> - An SQL fragment like "administrator = 1", <tt>["user_name = ?", username]</tt>,
        
      25. 
      
        
    25. 
          
          
              #   or <tt>["user_name = :user_name", { :user_name => user_name }]</tt>. See conditions in the intro.
        
      26. 
      
        
    26. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:order</tt> - An SQL fragment like "created_at DESC, name".
        
      27. 
      
        
    27. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:group</tt> - An attribute name by which the result should be grouped. Uses the <tt>GROUP BY</tt> SQL-clause.
        
      28. 
      
        
    28. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:having</tt> - Combined with +:group+ this can be used to filter the records that a
        
      29. 
      
        
    29. 
          
          
              #   <tt>GROUP BY</tt> returns. Uses the <tt>HAVING</tt> SQL-clause.
        
      30. 
      
        
    30. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:limit</tt> - An integer determining the limit on the number of rows that should be returned.
        
      31. 
      
        
    31. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:offset</tt> - An integer determining the offset from where the rows should be fetched. So at 5,
        
      32. 
      
        
    32. 
          
          
              #   it would skip rows 0 through 4.
        
      33. 
      
        
    33. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:joins</tt> - Either an SQL fragment for additional joins like "LEFT JOIN comments ON comments.post_id = id" (rarely needed),
        
      34. 
      
        
    34. 
          
          
              #   named associations in the same form used for the <tt>:include</tt> option, which will perform an
        
      35. 
      
        
    35. 
          
          
              #   <tt>INNER JOIN</tt> on the associated table(s),
        
      36. 
      
        
    36. 
          
          
              #   or an array containing a mixture of both strings and named associations.
        
      37. 
      
        
    37. 
          
          
              #   If the value is a string, then the records will be returned read-only since they will
        
      38. 
      
        
    38. 
          
          
              #   have attributes that do not correspond to the table's columns.
        
      39. 
      
        
    39. 
          
          
              #   Pass <tt>:readonly => false</tt> to override.
        
      40. 
      
        
    40. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:include</tt> - Names associations that should be loaded alongside. The symbols named refer
        
      41. 
      
        
    41. 
          
          
              #   to already defined associations. See eager loading under Associations.
        
      42. 
      
        
    42. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:select</tt> - By default, this is "*" as in "SELECT * FROM", but can be changed if you,
        
      43. 
      
        
    43. 
          
          
              #   for example, want to do a join but not include the joined columns. Takes a string with the SELECT SQL fragment (e.g. "id, name").
        
      44. 
      
        
    44. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:from</tt> - By default, this is the table name of the class, but can be changed
        
      45. 
      
        
    45. 
          
          
              #   to an alternate table name (or even the name of a database view).
        
      46. 
      
        
    46. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:readonly</tt> - Mark the returned records read-only so they cannot be saved or updated.
        
      47. 
      
        
    47. 
          
          
              # * <tt>:lock</tt> - An SQL fragment like "FOR UPDATE" or "LOCK IN SHARE MODE".
        
      48. 
      
        
    48. 
          
          
              #   <tt>:lock => true</tt> gives connection's default exclusive lock, usually "FOR UPDATE".
        
      49. 
      
        
    49. 
          
          
              #
        
      50. 
      
        
    50. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      51. 
      
        
    51. 
          
          
              #
        
      52. 
      
        
    52. 
          
          
              #   # find by id
        
      53. 
      
        
    53. 
          
          
              #   Person.find(1)       # returns the object for ID = 1
        
      54. 
      
        
    54. 
          
          
              #   Person.find(1, 2, 6) # returns an array for objects with IDs in (1, 2, 6)
        
      55. 
      
        
    55. 
          
          
              #   Person.find([7, 17]) # returns an array for objects with IDs in (7, 17)
        
      56. 
      
        
    56. 
          
          
              #   Person.find([1])     # returns an array for the object with ID = 1
        
      57. 
      
        
    57. 
          
          
              #   Person.where("administrator = 1").order("created_on DESC").find(1)
        
      58. 
      
        
    58. 
          
          
              #
        
      59. 
      
        
    59. 
          
          
              # Note that returned records may not be in the same order as the ids you
        
      60. 
      
        
    60. 
          
          
              # provide since database rows are unordered. Give an explicit <tt>:order</tt>
        
      61. 
      
        
    61. 
          
          
              # to ensure the results are sorted.
        
      62. 
      
        
    62. 
          
          
              #
        
      63. 
      
        
    63. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      64. 
      
        
    64. 
          
          
              #
        
      65. 
      
        
    65. 
          
          
              #   # find first
        
      66. 
      
        
    66. 
          
          
              #   Person.first # returns the first object fetched by SELECT * FROM people
        
      67.

      162. 
      
        
    162. 
          
          
              # Returns true if a record exists in the table that matches the +id+ or
        
      163. 
      
        
    163. 
          
          
              # conditions given, or false otherwise. The argument can take five forms:
        
      164. 
      
        
    164. 
          
          
              #
        
      165. 
      
        
    165. 
          
          
              # * Integer - Finds the record with this primary key.
        
      166. 
      
        
    166. 
          
          
              # * String - Finds the record with a primary key corresponding to this
        
      167. 
      
        
    167. 
          
          
              #   string (such as <tt>'5'</tt>).
        
      168. 
      
        
    168. 
          
          
              # * Array - Finds the record that matches these +find+-style conditions
        
      169. 
      
        
    169. 
          
          
              #   (such as <tt>['color = ?', 'red']</tt>).
        
      170. 
      
        
    170. 
          
          
              # * Hash - Finds the record that matches these +find+-style conditions
        
      171. 
      
        
    171. 
          
          
              #   (such as <tt>{:color => 'red'}</tt>).
        
      172. 
      
        
    172. 
          
          
              # * No args - Returns false if the table is empty, true otherwise.
        
      173. 
      
        
    173. 
          
          
              #
        
      174. 
      
        
    174. 
          
          
              # For more information about specifying conditions as a Hash or Array,
        
      175. 
      
        
    175. 
          
          
              # see the Conditions section in the introduction to ActiveRecord::Base.
        
      176. 
      
        
    176. 
          
          
              #
        
      177. 
      
        
    177. 
          
          
              # Note: You can't pass in a condition as a string (like <tt>name =
        
      178. 
      
        
    178. 
          
          
              # 'Jamie'</tt>), since it would be sanitized and then queried against
        
      179. 
      
        
    179. 
          
          
              # the primary key column, like <tt>id = 'name = \'Jamie\''</tt>.
        
      180. 
      
        
    180. 
          
          
              #
        
      181. 
      
        
    181. 
          
          
              # ==== Examples
        
      182. 
      
        
    182. 
          
          
              #   Person.exists?(5)
        
      183. 
      
        
    183. 
          
          
              #   Person.exists?('5')
        
      184. 
      
        
    184. 
          
          
              #   Person.exists?(:name => "David")
        
      185. 
      
        
    185. 
          
          
              #   Person.exists?(['name LIKE ?', "%#{query}%"])
        
      186. 
      
        
    186. 
          
          
              #   Person.exists?
        
      187. 
      
        
    187.

              # Specifies whether the records should be unique or not. For example:
        
      192.

              #
        
      193. 
      
        
    193. 
          
          
              #   User.select(:name)

      196.

              #   User.select(:name).uniq
        
      197.

              #   # => Returns 1 record per unique name
        
      198. 
      
        
    198. 
          
          
              #
        
      199. 
      
        
    199. 
          
          
              #   User.select(:name).uniq.uniq(false)
        
      200. 
      
        
    200. 
          
          
              #   # => You can also remove the uniqueness
        
      201.

    207. 
          
          
              # Used to extend a scope with additional methods, either through
        
      208. 
      
        
    208. 
          
          
              # a module or through a block provided.
        
      209. 
      
        
    209. 
          
          
              #
        
      210. 
      
        
    210. 
          
          
              # The object returned is a relation, which can be further extended.
        
      211. 
      
        
    211. 
          
          
              #
        
      212. 
      
        
    212. 
          
          
              # === Using a module
        
      213. 
      
        
    213. 
          
          
              #
        
      214. 
      
        
    214. 
          
          
              #   module Pagination
        
      215. 
      
        
    215. 
          
          
              #     def page(number)
        
      216. 
      
        
    216. 
          
          
              #       # pagination code goes here
        
      217. 
      
        
    217. 
          
          
              #     end
        
      218. 
      
        
    218. 
          
          
              #   end
        
      219. 
      
        
    219. 
          
          
              #
        
      220. 
      
        
    220. 
          
          
              #   scope = Model.scoped.extending(Pagination)
        
      221. 
      
        
    221. 
          
          
              #   scope.page(params[:page])
        
      222. 
      
        
    222. 
          
          
              #
        
      223. 
      
        
    223. 
          
          
              # You can also pass a list of modules:
        
      224. 
      
        
    224. 
          
          
              #
        
      225. 
      
        
    225. 
          
          
              #   scope = Model.scoped.extending(Pagination, SomethingElse)
        
      226. 
      
        
    226. 
          
          
              #
        
      227. 
      
        
    227. 
          
          
              # === Using a block
        
      228. 
      
        
    228. 
          
          
              #
        
      229. 
      
        
    229. 
          
          
              #   scope = Model.scoped.extending do
        
      230. 
      
        
    230. 
          
          
              #     def page(number)
        
      231. 
      
        
    231. 
          
          
              #       # pagination code goes here
        
      232. 
      
        
    232. 
          
          
              #     end
        
      233. 
      
        
    233. 
          
          
              #   end
        
      234. 
      
        
    234. 
          
          
              #   scope.page(params[:page])
        
      235. 
      
        
    235. 
          
          
              #
        
      236. 
      
        
    236. 
          
          
              # You can also use a block and a module list:
        
      237. 
      
        
    237. 
          
          
              #
        
      238. 
      
        
    238. 
          
          
              #   scope = Model.scoped.extending(Pagination) do
        
      239. 
      
        
    239. 
          
          
              #     def per_page(number)
        
      240. 
      
        
    240. 
          
          
              #       # pagination code goes here
        
      241. 
      
        
    241. 
          
          
              #     end
        
      242. 
      
        
    242. 
          
          
              #   end
        
      243. 
      
        
    243. 
          1

                return self if modules.empty?
        
      247.

      250.

                relation
        
      251.

              end

              def arel

              def build_arel
        
      264. 
      
        
    264. 
          13
          
                arel = table.from table
        
      265. 
      
        
    265. 
          
          
          
        
      266. 
      
        
    266. 
          13
          
                build_joins(arel, @joins_values) unless @joins_values.empty?
        
      267. 
      
        
    267. 
          
          
          
        
      268. 
      
        
    268. 
          13
          
                collapse_wheres(arel, (@where_values - ['']).uniq)
        
      269. 
      
        
    269. 
          
          
          
        
      270.

          13
          
                arel.having(*@having_values.uniq.reject{|h| h.blank?}) unless @having_values.empty?
        
      271.

      272.

          13
          
                arel.take(connection.sanitize_limit(@limit_value)) if @limit_value

          13
